As the Programmer, you should write a requirements.txt file, which is commonly used in Python projects to specify the dependencies or packages required for the project to run properly. It serves as a way to document and manage the project's dependencies in a standardized format. For example:

trading_bot.py
```python
'''
Contains the TradingBot class which implements the trading logic.
'''
import ccxt
class TradingBot:
    def __init__(self, api_key, api_secret, symbol, timeframe):
        self.exchange = ccxt.coindcx({
            'apiKey': api_key,
            'secret': api_secret
        })
        self.symbol = symbol
        self.timeframe = timeframe
        self.running = False
    def fetch_market_data(self):
        '''
        Fetches market data (OHLCV) for the specified symbol and timeframe.
        '''
        try:
            ohlcv = self.exchange.fetch_ohlcv(self.symbol, timeframe=self.timeframe)
            return ohlcv
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error fetching market data: {e}"
    def analyze_trend(self, ohlcv):
        '''
        Analyzes the market trend using a simple moving average strategy.
        Returns True if the current price is above the moving average, indicating an uptrend.
        '''
        closes = [candle[4] for candle in ohlcv]
        sma = sum(closes[-5:]) / 5
        current_price = closes[-1]
        return current_price > sma
    def execute_trade(self, trend):
        '''
        Executes a trade based on the analyzed trend.
        Buys if the trend is upward, sells otherwise.
        '''
        try:
            if trend:
                order = self.exchange.create_order(
                    symbol=self.symbol,
                    type='market',
                    side='buy',
                    amount=0.01  # Example amount, should be customizable
                )
                return f"Buy order executed: {order}"
            else:
                order = self.exchange.create_order(
                    symbol=self.symbol,
                    type='market',
                    side='sell',
                    amount=0.01  # Example amount, should be customizable
                )
                return f"Sell order executed: {order}"
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing trade: {e}"
    def customize_strategy(self, **kwargs):
        '''
        Allows customization of the trading strategy parameters.
        '''
        # Customize strategy parameters based on kwargs
        for key, value in kwargs.items():
            setattr(self, key, value)
    def start(self):
        '''
        Starts the trading bot, continuously fetching market data and executing trades.
        '''
        self.running = True
        while self.running:
            ohlcv = self.fetch_market_data()
            if isinstance(ohlcv, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                return ohlcv
            trend = self.analyze_trend(ohlcv)
            trade_result = self.execute_trade(trend)
            if isinstance(trade_result, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                return trade_result
    def stop(self):
        '''
        Stops the trading bot.
        '''
        self.running = False
```
gui.py
```python
'''
Contains the TradingBotGUI class to create and manage the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from trading_bot import TradingBot
class TradingBotGUI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Trading Bot")
        self.bot = None
        # Input fields for API key, secret, symbol, and timeframe
        tk.Label(self.root, text="API Key").pack()
        self.api_key_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.api_key_entry.pack()
        tk.Label(self.root, text="API Secret").pack()
        self.api_secret_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.api_secret_entry.pack()
        tk.Label(self.root, text="Symbol").pack()
        self.symbol_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.symbol_entry.pack()
        tk.Label(self.root, text="Timeframe").pack()
        self.timeframe_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.timeframe_entry.pack()
        # GUI components
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.root, text="Start Bot", command=self.start_bot)
        self.start_button.pack()
        self.stop_button = tk.Button(self.root, text="Stop Bot", command=self.stop_bot)
        self.stop_button.pack()
        self.status_label = tk.Label(self.root, text="Status: Stopped")
        self.status_label.pack()
    def start_bot(self):
        api_key = self.api_key_entry.get()
        api_secret = self.api_secret_entry.get()
        symbol = self.symbol_entry.get()
        timeframe = self.timeframe_entry.get()
        # Validate inputs
        if not api_key or not api_secret or not symbol or not timeframe:
            self.update_status("Invalid input")
            return
        self.bot = TradingBot(api_key, api_secret, symbol, timeframe)
        self.update_status("Running")
        while self.bot.running:
            ohlcv = self.bot.fetch_market_data()
            if isinstance(ohlcv, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                self.update_status(ohlcv)
                break
            trend = self.bot.analyze_trend(ohlcv)
            trade_result = self.bot.execute_trade(trend)
            if isinstance(trade_result, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                self.update_status(trade_result)
                break
    def stop_bot(self):
        if self.bot:
            self.bot.stop()
            self.update_status("Stopped")
    def update_status(self, status):
        self.status_label.config(text=f"Status: {status}")
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

trading_bot.py
```python
'''
Contains the TradingBot class which implements the trading logic.
'''
import ccxt
class TradingBot:
    def __init__(self, api_key, api_secret, symbol, timeframe):
        self.exchange = ccxt.coindcx({
            'apiKey': api_key,
            'secret': api_secret
        })
        self.symbol = symbol
        self.timeframe = timeframe
        self.running = False
    def fetch_market_data(self):
        '''
        Fetches market data (OHLCV) for the specified symbol and timeframe.
        '''
        try:
            ohlcv = self.exchange.fetch_ohlcv(self.symbol, timeframe=self.timeframe)
            return ohlcv
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error fetching market data: {e}"
    def analyze_trend(self, ohlcv):
        '''
        Analyzes the market trend using a simple moving average strategy.
        Returns True if the current price is above the moving average, indicating an uptrend.
        '''
        closes = [candle[4] for candle in ohlcv]
        sma = sum(closes[-5:]) / 5
        current_price = closes[-1]
        return current_price > sma
    def execute_trade(self, trend):
        '''
        Executes a trade based on the analyzed trend.
        Buys if the trend is upward, sells otherwise.
        '''
        try:
            if trend:
                order = self.exchange.create_order(
                    symbol=self.symbol,
                    type='market',
                    side='buy',
                    amount=0.01  # Example amount, should be customizable
                )
                return f"Buy order executed: {order}"
            else:
                order = self.exchange.create_order(
                    symbol=self.symbol,
                    type='market',
                    side='sell',
                    amount=0.01  # Example amount, should be customizable
                )
                return f"Sell order executed: {order}"
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error executing trade: {e}"
    def customize_strategy(self, **kwargs):
        '''
        Allows customization of the trading strategy parameters.
        '''
        # Customize strategy parameters based on kwargs
        for key, value in kwargs.items():
            setattr(self, key, value)
    def start(self):
        '''
        Starts the trading bot, continuously fetching market data and executing trades.
        '''
        self.running = True
        while self.running:
            ohlcv = self.fetch_market_data()
            if isinstance(ohlcv, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                return ohlcv
            trend = self.analyze_trend(ohlcv)
            trade_result = self.execute_trade(trend)
            if isinstance(trade_result, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                return trade_result
    def stop(self):
        '''
        Stops the trading bot.
        '''
        self.running = False
```

gui.py
```python
'''
Contains the TradingBotGUI class to create and manage the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from trading_bot import TradingBot
class TradingBotGUI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Trading Bot")
        self.bot = None
        # Input fields for API key, secret, symbol, and timeframe
        tk.Label(self.root, text="API Key").pack()
        self.api_key_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.api_key_entry.pack()
        tk.Label(self.root, text="API Secret").pack()
        self.api_secret_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.api_secret_entry.pack()
        tk.Label(self.root, text="Symbol").pack()
        self.symbol_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.symbol_entry.pack()
        tk.Label(self.root, text="Timeframe").pack()
        self.timeframe_entry = tk.Entry(self.root)
        self.timeframe_entry.pack()
        # GUI components
        self.start_button = tk.Button(self.root, text="Start Bot", command=self.start_bot)
        self.start_button.pack()
        self.stop_button = tk.Button(self.root, text="Stop Bot", command=self.stop_bot)
        self.stop_button.pack()
        self.status_label = tk.Label(self.root, text="Status: Stopped")
        self.status_label.pack()
    def start_bot(self):
        api_key = self.api_key_entry.get()
        api_secret = self.api_secret_entry.get()
        symbol = self.symbol_entry.get()
        timeframe = self.timeframe_entry.get()
        # Validate inputs
        if not api_key or not api_secret or not symbol or not timeframe:
            self.update_status("Invalid input")
            return
        self.bot = TradingBot(api_key, api_secret, symbol, timeframe)
        self.update_status("Running")
        while self.bot.running:
            ohlcv = self.bot.fetch_market_data()
            if isinstance(ohlcv, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                self.update_status(ohlcv)
                break
            trend = self.bot.analyze_trend(ohlcv)
            trade_result = self.bot.execute_trade(trend)
            if isinstance(trade_result, str):  # Check if an error message was returned
                self.update_status(trade_result)
                break
    def stop_bot(self):
        if self.bot:
            self.bot.stop()
            self.update_status("Stopped")
    def update_status(self, status):
        self.status_label.config(text=f"Status: {status}")
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
```

# Trading Bot User Manual

Welcome to the Trading Bot User Manual. This document will guide you through the installation, setup, and usage of the Trading Bot application, which is designed to execute trades on CoinDCX Futures using a trend-following strategy.

## Overview

The Trading Bot is a Python-based application that integrates with CoinDCX Futures to automate trading based on market trends. It utilizes a simple moving average strategy to determine market trends and executes trades accordingly. The application features a graphical user interface (GUI) for ease of use and allows for advanced customization options.

## Features

- **Trend-Following Strategy**: Utilizes a simple moving average to analyze market trends and make trading decisions.
- **Integration with CoinDCX Futures**: Connects to CoinDCX Futures using API keys for secure trading.
- **Customizable Parameters**: Allows users to customize trading parameters such as symbol, timeframe, and order amount.
- **Graphical User Interface**: Provides a user-friendly interface for inputting API credentials and controlling the bot.

## Installation

### Prerequisites

- Python 3.x
- An account on CoinDCX with API access

### Quick Install

1. **Clone the Repository**

   Clone the repository to your local machine using the following command:

   ```bash
   git clone <repository-url>
   ```

2. **Navigate to the Project Directory**

   ```bash
   cd <project-directory>
   ```

3. **Install Dependencies**

   Install the required Python packages using pip:

   ```bash
   pip install -r requirements.txt
   ```

   Ensure that `ccxt` is installed, as it is essential for interacting with the CoinDCX API.

## Usage

### Running the Application

1. **Start the Application**

   Run the main application file to launch the GUI:

   ```bash
   python main.py
   ```

2. **Input API Credentials**

   - Enter your CoinDCX API Key and Secret in the respective fields.
   - Specify the trading symbol (e.g., BTC/USDT) and the desired timeframe (e.g., 1m, 5m, 1h).

3. **Control the Bot**

   - Click "Start Bot" to initiate the trading bot. The bot will begin fetching market data, analyzing trends, and executing trades based on the strategy.
   - Click "Stop Bot" to halt the trading operations.

### Customizing the Strategy

The Trading Bot allows for customization of its trading strategy. You can modify parameters such as the order amount directly in the `trading_bot.py` file or through the GUI if additional fields are added for customization.

### Error Handling

The application includes basic error handling to manage issues such as invalid API credentials or network errors. Error messages will be displayed in the GUI status label.

## Support and Documentation

For further assistance, please refer to the source code comments and function docstrings for detailed explanations of the implementation. If you encounter any issues or have questions, feel free to reach out to the support team.

---

Thank you for choosing our Trading Bot. We hope it enhances your trading experience on CoinDCX Futures. Happy trading!
